  <raw>United States : US Stock-Index Futures Rise; AIG, Ford, Verizon Shares Climb




U.S. stock-index futures climbed, indicating the Standard &amp; Poor  s 500 Index will extend a four- week rally, before a report that may show consumer spending rose for a fifth consecutive month. 


American International Group Inc. added 1.3 percent in Germany after the insurer was said to have completed the $500 million sale of its PineBridge Investments. Ford Motor Co. climbed 1.3 percent as the carmaker agreed to sell its Volvo Cars unit. Alcoa Inc. led gains in commodity producers as metals prices rallied. 
Futures on the S&amp;P 500 expiring in June gained 0.5 percent to 1,169.50 as of 11:28 a.m. in London. The gauge has rallied for the last four weeks on speculation the economy is recovering from the worst contraction since the 1930s. Yields on 10-year Treasury notes climbed as high as 3.92 percent last week from a low of 3.53 percent in February. Dow Jones Industrial Average futures rose 0.4 percent to 10,839 and Nasdaq-100 Index futures advanced 0.5 percent to 1,961.25. 
The interest of investors is moving from bonds to equities,   said Robert Halver, head of research at Baader Bank in Frankfurt.   Economic data coming up today will point to further slow improvement in the U.S. economy. 
U.S. stocks rose on March 26 on analyst upgrades, takeover speculation and a European plan to help Greece avoid default before erasing most of the gain amid concern tension was escalating between North and South Korea. 
AIG added 1.3 percent to $34.64. The sale of the fund manager to Pacific Century Group after almost three months of delays was completed on March 26, according to two people with knowledge of the transaction. Lauren Day, a spokeswoman for the New York-based insurer, declined to comment. 
Ford, the only U.S. automaker that didn  t seek a federal rescue, rose 1.3 percent to $14.04 in early New York trading. Zhejiang Geely Holding Co. agreed to buy Volvo Cars from Ford for $1.8 billion in the biggest overseas acquisition by a Chinese automaker, more than 18 months after the two companies first entered discussions. 
The price includes a $200 million note and the remainder to be paid in cash, Ford Chief Financial Officer Lewis Booth said yesterday in Gothenburg, Sweden. Time spent on seeking regulatory approval in different jurisdictions means the companies now aim to complete the deal in the third quarter, Geely Chairman Li Shufu said.
Ltd.</raw>
